# big-code-k8s-bug-001: Missing ResourceSlice Event Handler in Kubernetes Scheduler

## Task

Investigate a bug in the Kubernetes scheduler where pods requesting Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) devices become permanently stuck in an Unschedulable state when the DRA driver starts after the pod is created. Trace the execution path through the scheduler's event-driven re-queuing architecture to identify why ResourceSlice creation/update events are silently dropped.

## Context

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.30.0 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/kubernetes--v1.30.0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (Go, ~3.5M LOC)
- **Category**: Bug Investigation
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Entry Point**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` — `ScheduleOne()` method

## Symptom

When a pod requests a DRA device and the DRA driver starts *after* the pod is created, the pod becomes permanently stuck in `Pending` with reason `Unschedulable`. The scheduler logs `"cannot allocate all claims"` because no ResourceSlices exist at scheduling time. After the driver starts and publishes ResourceSlice objects, the pod should be rescheduled — but it never is.

The bug is a race condition: if the driver starts first, scheduling succeeds immediately. But if the pod arrives before the driver, the scheduler never retries because ResourceSlice events are not wired into the scheduling queue's re-evaluation mechanism.

## Requirements

1. Starting from the entry point, trace the execution path to the root cause
2. Identify the specific file(s) and line(s) where the bug originates
3. Explain WHY the bug occurs — focus on the event handler registration mechanism and the scheduling queue's re-evaluation trigger
4. Propose a fix with specific code changes

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — examined for [reason]
- path/to/file2.ext — examined for [reason]
...

1. Symptom observed in: path/to/symptom.ext
2. Called from: path/to/caller.ext (function name)
3. Bug triggered by: path/to/buggy.ext (function name, line ~N)
...

## Root Cause
- **File**: path/to/root_cause.ext
- **Function**: function_name()
- **Line**: ~N
- **Explanation**: [Why this code is buggy]

## Proposed Fix
```diff
- buggy code
+ fixed code
```

[Detailed trace from symptom to root cause, explaining each step]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- Root cause identification: Did you find the correct file(s) where the bug originates?
- Call chain accuracy: Did you trace the correct path from symptom to root cause?
- Fix quality: Is the proposed fix correct and minimal?

## Summary

I've completed a comprehensive root cause analysis of the Kubernetes scheduler DRA ResourceSlice event handler bug. Here are the key findings:

### **Root Cause**
ResourceSlice events are completely missing from the scheduler's event-driven re-queuing architecture, causing pods requesting Dynamic Resource Allocation devices to become **permanently stuck** in an Unschedulable state when the DRA driver starts after the pod is created.

### **Bug Location - Three Missing Components**

1. **`pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (lines 68-96)**
   - Missing: `ResourceSlice GVK = "ResourceSlice"` constant
   - Cannot reference ResourceSlice in code without this

2. **`pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (lines 395-543)**
   - Missing: `case framework.ResourceSlice:` handler in the event registration switch statement
   - ResourceSlice changes never wake the scheduler queue

3. **`pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (lines 381-412)**
   - Missing: ResourceSlice in the `EventsToRegister()` method
   - Plugin doesn't know it should listen for ResourceSlice events

### **Why Pods Get Stuck**

The scheduler's re-queuing mechanism relies on plugins declaring which events should trigger pod re-evaluation. When a pod fails due to missing DRA resources:
1. Pod is moved to the unschedulable queue
2. When a ResourceSlice is created → event fired
3. **But no handler is registered** → event silently dropped
4. Queue never woken up → pod stays stuck forever

This only happens if the DRA driver starts *after* the pod (common during cluster initialization). If the driver starts first, ResourceSlices already exist and scheduling succeeds.

### **Proposed Fix**

Three coordinated changes:
- Add `ResourceSlice` GVK constant
- Register event handler for Res
... (truncated)

\\n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = \"\"}\n137: \n138: // schedulingCycle tries to schedule a single Pod.\n139: func (sched *Scheduler) schedulingCycle(\n140: \tctx context.Context,\n141: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n142: \tfwk *framework.Status) {\n147: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n148: \tpod := podInfo.Pod\n149: \tscheduleResult, err := sched.SchedulePod(ctx, fwk, state, pod)\n150: \tif err != nil {\n151: \t\tdefer func() {\n152: \t\t\tmetrics.SchedulingAlgorithmLatency.Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(start))\n153: \t\t}()\n154: \t\tif err == ErrNoNodesAvailable {\n155: \t\t\tstatus := framework.NewStatus(framework.UnschedulableAndUnresolvable).WithError(err)\n156: \t\t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, podInfo, status\n157: \t\t}\n158: \n159: \t\tfitError, clearNominatedNode}, podInfo, framework.AsStatus(err)\n163: \t\t}\n164: \n165: \t\t// SchedulePod() may have failed because the pod would not fit on any host, so we try to\n166: \t\t// preempt, with the expectation that the next time the pod is tried for scheduling it\n167: \t\t// will fit due to the preemption. It is also possible that a different pod will schedule\n168: \t\t// into the resources that were preempted, but this is harmless.\n169: \n170: \t\tif !fwk.HasPostFilterPlugins() {\n171: \t\t\tlogger.V(3).Info(\"No PostFilter plugins are registered, so no preemption will be performed\")\n172: \t\t\treturn ScheduleResult{}, podInfo, framework.NewStatus(framework.Unschedulable).WithError(err)\n173: \t\t}\n174: \n175: \t\t// Run PostFilter plugins to attempt to make the pod schedulable in a future scheduling cycle.\n176: \t\tresult, status := fwk.RunPostFilterPlugins(ctx, state, pod, fitError.Diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n177: \t\tmsg := status.Message()\n178: \t\tfitError.Diagnosis.PostFilterMsg = msg\n179: \t\tif \t\tif result != nil {\n187: \t\t\tnominatingInfo = result.NominatingInfo\n188: \t\t}\n189: \t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: nominatingInfo}, podInfo, framework.NewStatus(framework.Unschedulable).WithError(err)\n190: \t}\n191: \n192: \tmetrics.SchedulingAlgorithmLatency.Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(start))\n193: \t// Tell the cache to assume that a pod now is running on a given node, even though it hasn't been bound yet.\n194: \t// This allows us to keep scheduling without waiting on binding to occur.\n195: \tassumedPodInfo := podInfo.DeepCopy()\n196: \tassumedPod := assumedPodInfo.Pod\n197: \t// assume modifies `assumedPod` by setting NodeName=scheduleResult.SuggestedHost\n198: \terr = sched.assume(logger, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n199: \tif err != nil {\n200: \t\t// This is most probably result of a BUG in retrying logic.\n201: \t\t// We report an error here so that pod scheduling can be retried.\n202: \t\t// This relies on the fact that Error will check if the pod has been bound\n203: \t\t// to a node and if so will not add it back to the unscheduled pods queue\n204: \t\t// (otherwise this would cause an infinite loop).\n205: \t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, framework.AsStatus(err)\n206: \t}\n207: \n208: \t// Run the Reserve method of reserve plugins.\n209: \tif sts := fwk.RunReservePluginsReserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost); !sts.IsSuccess() {\n210: \t\t// trigger un-reserve to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n211: \t\tfwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n212: \t\tif forgetErr := sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\n213: \t\t\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \"Scheduler cache ForgetPod failed\")\n214: \t\t}\n215: \n216: \t\tif sts.IsRejected() {\n217: \t\t\tfitErr := &framework.FitError{\n218: \t\t\t\tNumAllNodes: 1,\n219: \t\t\t\tPod:         pod,\n220: \t\t\t\tDiagnosis: framework.Diagnosis{\n221: \t\t\t\t\tNodeToStatusMap: framework.NodeToStatusMap{scheduleResult.SuggestedHost: sts},\n222: \t\t\t\t},\n223: \t\t\t}\n224: \t\t\tfitErr.Diagnosis.AddPluginStatus(sts)\n225: \t\t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, framework.NewStatus(sts.Code()).WithError(fitErr)\n226: \t\t}\n227: \t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, sts\n228: \t}\n229: \n230: \t// Run \"permit\" plugins.\n231: \trunPermitStatus := fwk.RunPermitPlugins(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n232: \tif !runPermitStatus.IsWait() && !runPermitStatus.IsSuccess() {\n233: \t\t// sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\n236: \t\t\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \"Scheduler cache ForgetPod failed\")\n237: \t\t}\n238: \n239: \t\tif runPermitStatus.IsRejected() {\n240: \t\t\tfitErr := &framework.FitError{\n241: \t\t\t\tNumAllNodes: 1,\n242: \t\t\t\tPod:         pod,\n243: \t\t\t\tDiagnosis: framework.Diagnosis{\n244: \t\t\t\t\tNodeToStatusMap: framework.NodeToStatusMap{scheduleResult.SuggestedHost: runPermitStatus},\n245: \t\t\t\t},\n246: \t\t\t}\n247: \t\t\tfitErr.Diagnosis.AddPluginStatus(runPermitStatus)\n248: \t\t\treturn clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, runPermitStatus\n252: \t}\n253: \n254: \t// At the end of a successful scheduling cycle, pop and move up Pods if needed.\n255: \tif len(podsToActivate.Map) != 0 {\n256: \t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Activate(logger, podsToActivate.Map)\n257: \t\t// Clear the entries after activation.\n258: \t\tpodsToActivate.Map = make(map[string]*v1.Pod)\n259: \t}\n260: \n261: \treturn scheduleResult, assumedPodInfo, nil\n262: }\n263: \n264: // bindingCycle tries to bind an assumed Pod.\n265: func (sched *Scheduler) bindingCycle(\n266: \tctx context.Context,\n267: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n268: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n269: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n270: \tassumedPodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n271: \tstart time.Time,\n272: \tpodsToActivate *framework.PodsToActivate) *framework.Status {\n273: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n274: \n275: \tassumedPod := assumedPodInfo.Pod\n276: \n277: \t// Run \"permit\" plugins.\n278: \tif status := \t}\n302: \n303: \t// Calculating nodeResourceString can be heavy. \t\t// as `podsToActivate.Map` is no longer consumed.\n319: \t}\n320: \n321: \treturn nil\n322: }\n323: \n324: func (sched *Scheduler) handleBindingCycleError(\n325: \tctx context.Context,\n326: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n327: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n328: \tpodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n329: \tstart time.Time,\n330: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n331: \tstatus *framework.Status) {\n332: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n333: \n334: \tassumedPod := podInfo.Pod\n335: \t// trigger un-reserve plugins to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n336: internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, nil)\n352: \t\t}\n353: \t}\n354: \n355: \tsched.FailureHandler(ctx, fwk, podInfo, status, clearNominatedNode, start)\n356: }\n357: \n358: func (sched node list.\n388: // If it succeeds, it will return the name of the node.\n389: // If it fails, it will return a FitError with reasons.\n390: func (sched *Scheduler) schedulePod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (result ScheduleResult, err error) {\n391: \ttrace := utiltrace.New(\"Scheduling\", utiltrace.Field{Key: \"namespace\", Value: pod.Namespace}, utiltrace.Field{Key: \"name\", Value: pod.Name})\n392: \tdefer trace.LogIfLong(100 * time.Millisecond)\n393: \tif err := sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot(klog.FromContext(ctx), sched.nodeInfoSnapshot); err != nil {\n394: \t\treturn result, err\n395: \t}\n396: \ttrace.Step(\"Snapshotting scheduler cache and node infos done\")\n397: \n398: \tif \t\tFeasibleNodes:  len(feasibleNodes),\n437: \t}, err\n438: }\n439: \n440: // Filters the nodes to find the ones that fit the pod based on the framework\n441: // filter plugins and filter extenders.\n442: func (sched *Scheduler) findNodesThatFitPod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, framework.Diagnosis, error) {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := \t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins.Insert(framework.ExtenderName)\n524: \t}\n525: \n526: \treturn feasibleNodesAfterExtender, diagnosis, nil\n527: }\n528: \n529: func (sched *Scheduler) \n562: // hasExtenderFilters checks if any extenders filter nodes.\n563: func (sched *Scheduler) hasExtenderFilters() bool {\n564: \tfor _, extender := range sched.Extenders {\n565: \t\tif \t}\n596: \n597: \terrCh := parallelize.NewErrorChannel()\n598: \tvar feasibleNodesLen int32\n599: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n600: \tdefer cancel()\n601: \n602: \ttype nodeStatus struct {\n603: \t\tnode   string\n604: \t\tstatus *framework.Status\n605: \t}\n606: \tresult := make([]*nodeStatus, numAllNodes)\n607: \tcheckNode := func(i int) {\n608: \t\t// We check the nodes starting from where we left off in the previous scheduling cycle,\n609: \t\t// this is to make sure all nodes have the same chance of being examined across pods.\n610: \t\tnodeInfo := nodes[(sched.nextStartNodeIndex+i)%numAllNodes]\n611: \t\tstatus := fwk.RunFilterPluginsWithNominatedPods(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo)\n612: \t\tif status.Code() == framework.Error {\n613: \t\t\terrCh.SendErrorWithCancel(status.AsError(), cancel)\n614: \t\t\treturn\n615: \t\t}\n616: \t\tif status.IsSuccess() {\n617: \t\t\tlength := atomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, 1)\n618: \t\t\tif length > numNodesToFind {\n619: \t\t\t\tcancel()\n620: \t\t\t\tatomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, -1)\n621: \t\t\t} else {\n622: \t\t\t\tfeasibleNodes[length-1] = nodeInfo\n623: \t\t\t}\n624: \t\t} else {\n625: \t\t\tresult[i] = &nodeStatus{node: nodeInfo.Node().Name, status: status}\n626: \t\t}\n627: \t}\n628: \n629: \tbeginCheckNode := time.Now()\n630: \tstatusCode := framework.Success\n631: \tdefer func() {\n632: \t\t// We record Filter extension point latency here instead of in framework.go because framework.RunFilterPlugins\n633: \t\t// function is called for each node, whereas we want to have an overall latency for all nodes per scheduling cycle.\n634: \t\t// Note that this latency also includes latency for `addNominatedPods`, which calls framework.RunPreFilterAddPod.\n635: \t\tmetrics.FrameworkExtensionPointDuration.WithLabelValues(metrics.Filter, statusCode.String(), fwk.ProfileName()).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(beginCheckNode))\n636: \t}()\n637: \n638: \t// Stops searching for more nodes once the configured number of feasible nodes\n639: \t// are found.\n640: \tfwk.Parallelizer().Until(ctx, numAllNodes, checkNode, metrics.Filter)\n641: \tfeasibleNodes = feasibleNodes[:feasibleNodesLen]\n642: \tfor _, item := range result {\n643: \t\tif item == nil {\n644: \t\t\tcontinue\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[item.node] = item.status\n647: \t\tdiagnosis.AddPluginStatus(item.status)\n648: \t}\n649: \tif err := errCh.ReceiveError(); err != nil {\n650: \t\tstatusCode = framework.Error\n651: \t\treturn feasibleNodes, err\n652: \t}\n653: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n654: }\n655: \n656: // numFeasibleNodesToFind returns the number of feasible nodes that once found, the scheduler stops\n657: // its search for more feasible nodes.\n658: func (sched *Scheduler) numFeasibleNodesToFind(percentageOfNodesToScore *int32, numAllNodes int32) (numNodes int32) {\n659: \tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n660: \t\treturn numAllNodes\n661: \t}\n662: \n663: \t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. Otherwise, use global percentageOfNodesToScore.\n664: \tvar percentage int32\n665: \tif percentageOfNodesToScore != nil {\n666: \t\tpercentage = *percentageOfNodesToScore\n667: \t} else {\n668: \t\tpercentage = sched.percentageOfNodesToScore\n669: \t}\n670: \n671: \tif percentage == 0 {\n672: \t\tpercentage = int32(50) - numAllNodes/125\n673: \t\tif percentage < minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind {\n674: \t\t\tpercentage = minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind\n675: \t\t}\n676: \t}\n677: \n678: \tnumNodes = numAllNodes * percentage / 100\n679: \tif numNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n680: \t\treturn minFeasibleNodesToFind\n681: \t}\n682: \n683: \treturn numNodes\n684: }\n685: \n686: func findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx context.Context, extenders []framework.Extender, pod *v1.Pod, feasibleNodes []*framework.NodeInfo, statuses framework.NodeToStatusMap) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n687: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n688: \t// Extenders are called sequentially.\n689: \t// Nodes in original feasibleNodes can be excluded in one extender, and pass on to the next\n690: \t// extender in a decreasing manner.\n691: \tfor _, for\n701: \t\t// particular nodes, and this may eventually improve preemption efficiency.\n702: \t\t// Note: users are recommended to configure the extenders that may return \t\t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t\t}\n710: \t\t\treturn nil, err\n711: \t\t}\n712: \n713: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedAndUnresolvableMap {\n714: \t\t\tvar aggregatedReasons \t\t\t}\n733: \t\t}\n734: \n735: \t\tfeasibleNodes = feasibleList\n736: \t}\n737: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n738: }\n739: \n740: // prioritizeNodes prioritizes the nodes by running the score plugins,\n741: // which return a score for each node from the call to RunScorePlugins().\n742: // The scores from each plugin are added together to make the score for that node, then\n743: // any extenders are run as well.\n744: // All scores are finally combined (added) to get the total weighted scores of all nodes\n745: func prioritizeNodes(\n746: \tctx context.Context,\n747: \textenders []framework.Extender,\n748: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n749: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n750: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n751: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo,\n752: ) ([]framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\n753: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n754: \t// If no priority configs are provided, then all nodes will have a score of one.\n755: \t// This is required to generate the priority list in the nodesScores, nil\n855: }\n856: \n857: var errEmptyPriorityList = errors.New(\"empty priorityList\")\n858: \n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\n864: \tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\n865: \t\treturn \"\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\n866: \t}\n867: \n868: \tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\n869: \theap.Init(&h)\n870: \tcntOfMaxScore := 1\n871: \tselectedIndex := 0\n872: \t// The top of the heap is the NodeScoreResult with the highest score.\n873: \tsortedNodeScoreList := make([]framework.NodePluginScores, 0, count)\n874: \tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores))\n875: \n876: \t// This for-loop will continue until all Nodes with the highest scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\n877: \t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\n878: \tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores) {\n879: \t\tif ns.TotalScore != sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore && len(sortedNodeScoreList) == count {\n880: \t\t\tbreak\n881: \t\t}\n882: \n883: \t\tif ns.TotalScore == sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore {\n884: \t\t\tcntOfMaxScore++\n885: \t\t\tif rand.Intn(cntOfMaxScore) == 0 {\n886: \t\t\t\t// Replace the candidate with probability of 1/cntOfMaxScore\n887: \t\t\t\tselectedIndex = cntOfMaxScore - 1\n888: \t\t\t}\n889: \t\t}\n890: \n891: \t\tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, ns)\n892: \n893: \t\tif h.Len() == 0 {\n894: \t\t\tbreak\n895: \t\t}\n896: \t}\n897: \n898: \tif selectedIndex != 0 {\n899: \t\t// replace the first one with selected one\n900: \t\tprevious := sortedNodeScoreList[0]\n901: \t\tsortedNodeScoreList[0] = sortedNodeScoreList[selectedIndex]\n902: \t\tsortedNodeScoreList[selectedIndex] = previous\n903: \t}\n904: \n905: \tif len(sortedNodeScoreList) > count {\n906: \t\tsortedNodeScoreList = sortedNodeScoreList[:count]\n907: \t}\n908: \n909: \treturn sortedNodeScoreList[0].Name, sortedNodeScoreList, nil\n910: }\n911: \n912: // nodeScoreHeap is a heap of framework.NodePluginScores.\n913: type nodeScoreHeap []framework.NodePluginScores\n914: \n915: // nodeScoreHeap implements heap.Interface.\n916: var _ heap.Interface = &nodeScoreHeap{}\n917: \n918: func (h nodeScoreHeap) Len() int           { return len(h) }\n919: func (h nodeScoreHeap) Less(i, j int) bool { return h[i].TotalScore > h[j].TotalScore }\n920: func (h nodeScoreHeap) Swap(i, j int)      { h[i], h[j] = h[j], h[i] }\n921: \n922: func (h *nodeScoreHeap) Push(x interface{}) {\n923: \t*h = append(*h, x.(framework.NodePluginScores))\n924: }\n925: \n926: func (h *nodeScoreHeap) Pop() interface{} {\n927: \told := *h\n928: \tn := succeed and send it to apiserver\n938: \t// in the background.\n939: \t// If the binding fails, scheduler will release resources allocated to assumed pod\n940: \t// immediately.\n941: \n990: func (sched *Scheduler) finishBinding(logger klog.Logger, fwk framework.Framework, assumed *v1.Pod, targetNode string, status *framework.Status) {\n991: \tif finErr := \t}\n1008: \treturn strconv.Itoa(p.Attempts)\n1009: }\n1010: \n1011: // handleSchedulingFailure records an event for the pod that indicates the\n1012: // pod has failed to schedule. Also, update the pod condition and nominated node name if set.\n1013: func (sched *Scheduler) handleSchedulingFailure(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, podInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo, status *framework.Status, nominatingInfo *framework.NominatingInfo, start time.Time) {\n1014: \tcalledDone := false\n1015: \tdefer func() {\n1016: \t\tif !calledDone {\n1017: \t\t\t// Basically, AddUnschedulableIfNotPresent calls DonePod internally.\n1018: \t\t\t// But, AddUnschedulableIfNotPresent isn't called in some corner cases.\n1019: \t\t\t// Here, we call DonePod explicitly to avoid leaking the pod.\n1020: \t\t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Done(podInfo.Pod.UID)\n1021: \t\t}\n1022: \t}()\n1023: \n1024: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n1025: \treason := v1.PodReasonSchedulerError\n1026: \tif status.IsRejected() {\n1027: \t\treason = v1.PodReasonUnschedulable\n1028: \t}\n1029: \n1030: \tswitch reason {\n1031: \tcase v1.PodReasonUnschedulable:\n1032: \t\tmetrics.PodUnschedulable(fwk.ProfileName(), metrics.SinceInSeconds(start))\n1033: \tcase v1.PodReasonSchedulerError:\n1034: \t\tmetrics.PodScheduleError(fwk.ProfileName(), metrics.SinceInSeconds(start))\n1035: \t}\n1036: \n1037: \tpod := podInfo.Pod\n1038: \terr := status.AsError()\n1039: \terrMsg := status.Message()\n1040: \n1041: \tif err == ErrNoNodesAvailable {\n1042: \t\tlogger.V(2).Info(\"Unable to schedule pod; SSA is safe because only\n205: \t\t\t// the scheduler updates these fields.\n206: \t\t\tspec := resourcev1alpha2apply.PodSchedulingContextSpec()\n207: \t\t\tspec.SelectedNode = p.selectedNode\n208: \t\t\tif p.potentialNodes != nil {\n209: \t\t\t\tspec.PotentialNodes = *p.potentialNodes\n210: \t\t\t} else {\n211: \t\t\t\t// Unchanged. Has to be set because the object that we send\n212: \t\t\t\t// must represent the \"fully specified intent\". Not sending\n213: \t\t\t\t// the list would clear it.\n214: \t\t\t\tspec.PotentialNodes = p.schedulingCtx.Spec.PotentialNodes\n215: \t\t\t}\n216: \t\t\tschedulingCtxApply := resourcev1alpha2apply.PodSchedulingContext(pod.Name, pod.Namespace).WithSpec(spec)\n217: \n218: \t\t\tif loggerV := logger.V(6); loggerV.Enabled() {\n219: \t\t\t\t// At a high enough log level, dump the entire object.\n220: \t\t\t\tloggerV.Info(\"Patching PodSchedulingContext\", \"podSchedulingCtx\", klog.KObj(pod), \"podSchedulingCtxApply\", klog.Format(schedulingCtxApply))\n221: \t\t\t} else {\n222: \t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Patching PodSchedulingContext\", \"podSchedulingCtx\", klog.KObj(pod))\n223: \t\t\t}\n224: \t\t\t_, err = clientset.ResourceV1alpha2().PodSchedulingContexts(pod.Namespace).Apply(ctx, schedulingCtxApply, metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"kube-scheduler\", Force: true})\n225: \t\t}\n226: \n227: \t} else {\n228: \t\t// Create it.\n229: \t\tschedulingCtx := &resourcev1alpha2.PodSchedulingContext{\n230: \t\t\tObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{\n231: \t\t\t\tName:            pod.Name,\n232: \t\t\t\tNamespace:       pod.Namespace,\n233: \t\t\t\tOwnerReferences: []metav1.OwnerReference{*metav1.NewControllerRef(pod, schema.GroupVersionKind{Version: \"v1\", Kind: \"Pod\"})},\n234: \t\t\t},\n235: \t\t}\n236: \t\tif p.selectedNode != nil {\n237: \t\t\tschedulingCtx.Spec.SelectedNode = *p.selectedNode\n238: \t\t}\n239: \t\tif p.potentialNodes != nil {\n240: \t\t\tschedulingCtx.Spec.PotentialNodes = *p.potentialNodes\n241: \t\t}\n242: \t\tif loggerV := logger.V(6); loggerV.Enabled() {\n243: \t\t\t// At a high enough log level, dump the entire object.\n244: \t\t\tloggerV.Info(\"Creating PodSchedulingContext\", \"podSchedulingCtx\", klog.KObj(schedulingCtx), \"podSchedulingCtxObject\", klog.Format(schedulingCtx))\n245: \t\t} else {\n246: clientset.ResourceV1alpha2().PodSchedulingContexts(schedulingCtx.Namespace).Create(ctx, schedulingCtx, metav1.CreateOptions{})\n249: \t}\n250: \tif err != nil {\n251: \t\treturn err\n252: \t}\n253: \tp.potentialNodes = nil\n254: \tp.selectedNode = nil\n255: \treturn nil\n256: }\n257: \n258: func statusForClaim(schedulingCtx *resourcev1alpha2.PodSchedulingContext, podClaimName string) *resourcev1alpha2.ResourceClaimSchedulingStatus {\n259: \tif schedulingCtx == nil {\n260: \t\treturn nil\n261: \t}\n262: \tfor _, status := range schedulingCtx.Status.ResourceClaims {\n263: \t\tif status.Name == podClaimName {\n264: \t\t\treturn &status\n265: \t\t}\n266: \t}\n267: \treturn nil\n268: }\n269: \n270: // dynamicResources is a plugin that ensures that ResourceClaims are allocated.\n271: type dynamicResources struct {\n272: \tenabled                    bool\n273: \tfh                         framework.Handle\n274: \tclientset                  kubernetes.Interface\n275: \tclaimLister                resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClaimLister\n276: \tclassLister                resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClassLister\n277: \tpodSchedulingContextLister resourcev1alpha2listers.PodSchedulingContextLister\n278: \tclaimParametersLister      resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClaimParametersLister\n279: \tclassParametersLister      resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClassParametersLister\n280: \tresourceSliceLister        resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceSliceLister\n281: \tclaimNameLookup            *resourceclaim.Lookup\n282: \n283: \t// claimAssumeCache enables temporarily storing a newer claim object\n284: \t// while the scheduler has allocated it and the corresponding object\n285: \t// update from the apiserver has not been processed by the claim\n286: \t// informer callbacks. Claims get added here in PreBind and removed by\n287: \t// the informer callback (based on the \"newer than\" comparison in the\n288: \t// assume cache).\n289: \t//\n290: \t// It uses cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc to generate object names, which\n291: \t// therefore are \"<namespace>/<name>\".\n292: \t//\n293: \t// This is necessary to ensure that reconstructing the resource usage\n294: \t// at the start of a pod scheduling cycle doesn't reuse the resources\n295: \t// assigned to such a claim. Alternatively, claim allocation state\n296: \t// could also get tracked across pod scheduling cycles, but that\n297: \t// - adds complexity (need to carefully sync state with informer events\n298: \t//   for claims and ResourceSlices)\n299: \t// - would make integration with cluster autoscaler harder because it would need\n300: \t//   to trigger informer callbacks.\n301: \t//\n302: \t// When implementing cluster autoscaler support, this assume cache or\n303: \t// something like it (see https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/112202)\n304: \t// might have to be managed by the cluster autoscaler.\n305: \tclaimAssumeCache volumebinding.AssumeCache\n306: \n307: \t// inFlightAllocations is map from claim UUIDs to claim objects for those claims\n308: \t// for which allocation was triggered during a scheduling cycle and the\n309: \t// corresponding claim status update call in PreBind has not been done\n310: \t// yet. If another pod needs the claim, the pod is treated as \"not\n311: \t// schedulable yet\". The cluster event for the claim status update will\n312: \t// make it schedulable.\n313: \t//\n314: \t// This mechanism avoids the following problem:\n315: \t// - Pod A triggers allocation for claim X.\n316: \t// - Pod B shares access to that claim and gets scheduled because\n317: \t//   the claim is assumed to be allocated.\n318: \t// - PreBind for pod B is called first, tries to update reservedFor and\n319: \t//   fails because the claim is not really allocated yet.\n320: \t//\n321: \t// We could avoid the ordering problem by allowing either pod A or pod B\n322: \t// to set the allocation. But that is more complicated and leads to another\n323: \t// problem:\n324: \t// - Pod A and B get scheduled as above.\n325: \t// - PreBind for pod A gets called first, then fails with a temporary API error.\n326: \t//   It removes the updated claim from the assume cache because of that.\n327: \t// - PreBind for pod B gets called next and succeeds with adding the\n328: \t//   allocation and its own reservedFor entry.\n329: \t// - The assume cache is now not reflecting that the claim is allocated,\n330: \t//   which could lead to reusing the same resource for some other claim.\n331: \t//\n332: \t// A sync.Map is used because in practice sharing of a claim between\n333: \t// pods is expected to be rare compared to per-pod claim, so we end up\n334: \t// hitting the \"multiple goroutines read, write, and overwrite entries\n335: \t// for disjoint sets of keys\" case that sync.Map is optimized for.\n336: \tinFlightAllocations sync.Map\n337: }\n338: \n339: // New initializes a new plugin and returns it.\n340: func New(ctx context.Context, plArgs runtime.Object, fh framework.Handle, fts feature.Features) (framework.Plugin, error) {\n341: \tif !fts.EnableDynamicResourceAllocation {\n342: \t\t// Disabled, won't do anything.\n343: \t\treturn &dynamicResources{}, nil\n344: \t}\n345: \n346: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n347: \tpl := &dynamicResources{\n348: \t\tenabled:                    true,\n349: \t\tfh:                         fh,\n350: \t\tclientset:                  fh.ClientSet(),\n351: \t\tclaimLister:                fh.SharedInformerFactory().Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClaims().Lister(),\n352: \t\tclassLister:                fh.SharedInformerFactory().Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClasses().Lister(),\n353: \t\tpodSchedulingContextLister: fh.SharedInformerFactory().Resource().V1alpha2().PodSchedulingContexts().Lister(),\n354: \t\tclaimParametersLister:      fh.SharedInformerFactory().Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClaimParameters().Lister(),\n355: \t\tclassParametersLister:      fh.SharedInformerFactory().Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Lister(),\n356: \t\tresourceSliceLister:        fh.SharedInformerFactory().Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Lister(),\n357: \t\tclaimNameLookup:            resourceclaim.NewNameLookup(fh.ClientSet()),\n358: \t\tclaimAssumeCache:           volumebinding.NewAssumeCache(logger, fh.SharedInformerFactory().Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClaims().Informer(), \"claim\", \"\", nil),\n359: \t}\n360: \n361: \treturn pl, nil\n362: }\n363: \n364: var _ framework.PreEnqueuePlugin = &dynamicResources{}\n365: var _ framework.PreFilterPlugin = &dynamicResources{}\n366: var _ framework.FilterPlugin = &dynamicResources{}\n367: var _ framework.PostFilterPlugin = &dynamicResources{}\n368: var _ framework.PreScorePlugin = &dynamicResources{}\n369: var _ framework.ReservePlugin = &dynamicResources{}\n370: var _ by this plugin schedulable.\n381: func (pl *dynamicResources) EventsToRegister() []framework.ClusterEventWithHint {\n382: \tif !pl.enabled {\n383: \t\treturn nil\n384: \t}\n385: \n386: \tevents := []framework.ClusterEventWithHint{\n387: \t\t// Changes for claim or class parameters creation may make pods\n388: \t\t// schedulable which depend on claims using those parameters.\n389: \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimParametersChange},\n390: \t\t{Event: scenario,\n403: \t\t// when a node is added but not ready, NodeAdd event is filtered out by preCheck and doesn't arrive.\n404: \t\t// In such cases, this plugin may miss some events that actually make framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n411: \t}\n412: \treturn events\n413: }\n414: \n415: // PreEnqueue checks if there are known reasons why a pod currently cannot be\n416: // scheduled. The delete claim event will not invoke it, so newObj will never be nil.\n429: func (pl *dynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterClaimParametersChange(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (framework.QueueingHint, error) {\n430: \toriginalParameters, modifiedParameters, err := schedutil.As[*resourcev1alpha2.ResourceClaimParameters](oldObj, newObj)\n431: \tif err != nil {\n432: \t\t// Shouldn't happen.\n433: \t\treturn framework.Queue, fmt.Errorf(\"unexpected object in isSchedulableAfterClaimParametersChange: %w\", err)\n434: \t}\n435: \n436: \tusesParameters := false\n437: \tif err := pl.foreachPodResourceClaim(pod, func(_ string, claim *resourcev1alpha2.ResourceClaim) {\n438: \t\tref := claim.Spec.ParametersRef\n439: \t\tif ref == nil {\n440: \t\t\treturn\n441: \t\t}\n442: \n443: \t\t// Using in-tree parameters directly?\n444: \t\tif ref.APIGroup == resourcev1alpha2.SchemeGroupVersion.Group &&\n445: \t\t\tref.Kind == \"ResourceClaimParameters\" {\n446: \t\t\tif modifiedParameters.Name == ref.Name {\n447: \t\t\t\tusesParameters = true\n448: \t\t\t}\n449: \t\t\treturn\n450: \t\t}\n451: \n452: \t\t// Need to look for translated parameters.\n453: \t\tgeneratedFrom := modifiedParameters.GeneratedFrom\n454: \t\tif generatedFrom == nil {\n455: \t\t\treturn\n456: \t\t}\n457: \t\tif generatedFrom.APIGroup == ref.APIGroup &&\n458: \t\t\tgeneratedFrom.Kind == ref.Kind &&\n459: \t\t\tgeneratedFrom.Name == ref.Name {\n460: \t\t\tusesParameters = true\n461: \t\t}\n462: \t}); The delete claim event will not invoke it, so newObj will never be nil.\n572: func (pl *dynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterClaimChange(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (framework.QueueingHint, error) {\n573: \toriginalClaim, modifiedClaim, err := schedutil.As[*resourcev1alpha2.ResourceClaim](oldObj, newObj)\n574: \tif err != nil {\n575: \t\t// Shouldn't happen.\n576: \t\treturn framework.Queue, fmt.Errorf(\"unexpected object in isSchedulableAfterClaimChange: %w\", err)\n577: \t}\n578: \n579: \tusesClaim := false\n580: \tif err := pl.foreachPodResourceClaim(pod, func(_ string, claim *resourcev1alpha2.ResourceClaim) {\n581: \t\tif claim.UID == modifiedClaim.UID {\n582: \t\t\tusesClaim = true\n583: \t\t}\n584: \t}); err != nil {\n585: \t\t// This is not an unexpected error: we know that\n586: \t\t// foreachPodResourceClaim only returns errors for \"not\n587: \t\t// schedulable\".\n588: \t\tlogger.V(4).Info(\"pod is not schedulable\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"claim\", klog.KObj(modifiedClaim), \"reason\", err.Error())\n589: \t\treturn framework.QueueSkip, nil\n590: \t}\n591: \n592: \tif originalClaim != nil &&\n593: \t\tresourceclaim.IsAllocatedWithStructuredParameters(originalClaim) &&\n594: \t\tmodifiedClaim.Status.Allocation == nil {\n595: \t\t// A claim with structured parameters was deallocated. This might have made\n596: \t\t// resources available for other pods.\n597: \t\t//\n598: \t\t// TODO (https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/123697):\n599: \t\t// check that the pending claims depend on structured parameters (depends on refactoring foreachPodResourceClaim, see other TODO).\n600: \t\t//\n601: \t\t// There is a small race here:\n602: \t\t// - The dynamicresources plugin allocates claim A and updates the assume cache.\n603: \t\t// - A second pod gets marked as unschedulable based on that assume cache.\n604: \t\t// - Before the informer cache here catches up, the pod runs, terminates and\n605: \t\t//   the claim gets deallocated without ever sending the claim status with\n606: \t\t//   allocation to the scheduler.\n607: \t\t// - The comparison below is for a *very* old claim with no allocation and the\n608: \t\t//   new claim where the allocation is already removed again, so no\n609: \t\t//   RemovedClaimAllocation event gets emitted.\n610: \t\t//\n611: \t\t// This is extremely unlikely and thus a fix is not needed for alpha in Kubernetes 1.30.\n612: \t\t// TODO (https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/123698): The solution is to somehow integrate the assume cache\n613: \t\t// into the event mechanism. If the entire\n631: \t// status is as before, then something else must have changed\n632: \t// and we don't care. What happens in practice is that the\n633: \t// resource driver adds the finalizer.\n634: \tif apiequality.Semantic.DeepEqual(&originalClaim.Status, &modifiedClaim.Status) {\n635: \t\tif loggerV := logger.V(7); loggerV.Enabled() {\n636: \t\t\t// Log more information.\n637: \t\t\tloggerV.Info(\"claim for pod got modified where the pod doesn't care\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"claim\", klog.KObj(modifiedClaim), \"diff\", cmp.Diff(originalClaim, modifiedClaim))\n638: \t\t} else {\n639: \t\t\tlogger.V(6).Info(\"claim for pod got modified where the pod doesn't care\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"claim\", klog.KObj(modifiedClaim))\n640: \t\t}\n641: \t\treturn framework.QueueSkip, nil\n642: \t}\n643: \n644: \tlogger.V(4).Info(\"status of claim for pod got updated\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"claim\", klog.KObj(modifiedClaim))\n645: \treturn framework.Queue, nil\n646: }\n647: \n648: // isSchedulableAfterPodSchedulingContextChange is invoked for all\n649: // PodSchedulingContext events reported by an informer. It checks whether that\n650: // change made a previously unschedulable pod schedulable (updated) or a new\n651: // attempt is needed to re-create the object (deleted). It errs on the side of\n652: // letting a pod scheduling attempt happen.\n653: func (pl *dynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterPodSchedulingContextChange(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (framework.QueueingHint, error) {\n654: \t// Deleted? That can happen because we ourselves delete the PodSchedulingContext while\n655: \t// working on the pod. This can be ignored.\n656: \tif oldObj != nil && newObj == nil {\n657: \t\tlogger.V(4).Info(\"PodSchedulingContext got deleted\")\n658: \t\treturn framework.QueueSkip, nil\n659: \t}\n660: \n661: \toldPodScheduling, newPodScheduling, err := schedutil.As[*resourcev1alpha2.PodSchedulingContext](oldObj, newObj)\n662: \tif err != nil {\n663: \t\t// Shouldn't happen.\n664: \t\treturn framework.Queue, fmt.Errorf(\"unexpected object in isSchedulableAfterPodSchedulingContextChange: %w\", err)\n665: \t}\n666: \tpodScheduling := newPodScheduling // Never nil because deletes are handled above.\n667: \n668: \tif podScheduling.Name != pod.Name || podScheduling.Namespace != pod.Namespace {\n669: \t\tlogger.V(7).Info(\"PodSchedulingContext for unrelated pod got modified\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"podScheduling\", klog.KObj(podScheduling))\n670: \t\treturn framework.QueueSkip, nil\n671: \t}\n672: \n673: \t// If the drivers have provided information about all\n674: \t// unallocated claims with delayed allocation, then the next\n675: \t// scheduling attempt is able to pick a node, so we let it run\n676: \t// immediately if this occurred for the first time, otherwise\n677: \t// we allow backoff.\n678: \tpendingDelayedClaims := 0\n679: \tif err := pl.foreachPodResourceClaim(pod, func(podResourceName string, claim *resourcev1alpha2.ResourceClaim) {\n680: \t\tif claim.Spec.AllocationMode == resourcev1alpha2.AllocationModeWaitForFirstConsumer &&\n681: \t\t\tclaim.Status.Allocation == nil &&\n682: \t\t\t!podSchedulingHasClaimInfo(podScheduling, podResourceName) {\n683: \t\t\tpendingDelayedClaims++\n684: \t\t}\n685: \t}); err != nil {\n686: \t\t// This is not an unexpected error: we know that\n687: \t\t// foreachPodResourceClaim only returns errors for \"not\n688: \t\t// schedulable\".\n689: \t\tlogger.V(4).Info(\"pod is not schedulable, keep waiting\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"reason\", err.Error())\n690: \t\treturn framework.QueueSkip, nil\n691: \t}\n692: \n693: \t// Some driver responses missing?\n694: \tif pendingDelayedClaims > 0 {\n695: \t\t// We could start a pod scheduling attempt to refresh the\n696: \t\t// potential nodes list.  But pod scheduling attempts are\n697: \t\t// expensive and doing them too often causes the pod to enter\n698: \t\t// backoff. Let's wait instead for all drivers to reply.\n699: \t\tif loggerV := logger.V(6); loggerV.Enabled() {\n700: \t\t\tloggerV.Info(\"PodSchedulingContext with missing resource claim information, keep waiting\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"podSchedulingDiff\", cmp.Diff(oldPodScheduling, podScheduling))\n701: \t\t} else {\n702: \t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"PodSchedulingContext with missing resource claim information, keep waiting\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod))\n703: \t\t}\n704: \t\treturn framework.QueueSkip, nil\n705: \t}\n706: \n707: \tif oldPodScheduling == nil /* create */ ||\n708: \t\tlen(oldPodScheduling.Status.ResourceClaims) < len(podScheduling.Status.ResourceClaims) /* new information and not incomplete (checked above) */ {\n709: \t\t// This definitely is new information for the scheduler. Try again immediately.\n710: \t\tlogger.V(4).Info(\"PodSchedulingContext for pod has all required information, schedule immediately\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod))\n711: \t\treturn framework.Queue, nil\n712: \t}\n713: \n714: \t// The other situation where the scheduler needs to do\n715: \t// something immediately is when the selected node doesn't\n716: \t// work: waiting in the backoff queue only helps eventually\n717: \t// resources on the selected node become available again. It's\n718: \t// much more likely, in particular when trying to fill up the\n719: \t// cluster, that the choice simply didn't work out. The risk\n720: \t// here is that in a situation where the cluster really is\n721: \t// full, backoff won't be used because the scheduler keeps\n722: \t// trying different nodes. This should not happen when it has\n723: \t// full knowledge about resource availability (=\n724: \t// PodSchedulingContext.*.UnsuitableNodes is complete) but may happen\n725: \t// when it doesn't (= PodSchedulingContext.*.UnsuitableNodes had to be\n726: \t// truncated).\n727: \t//\n728: \t// Truncation only happens for very large clusters and then may slow\n729: \t// down scheduling, but should not break it completely. This is\n730: \t// acceptable while DRA is alpha and will be investigated further\n731: \t// before moving DRA to beta.\n732: \tif podScheduling.Spec.SelectedNode != \"\" {\n733: \t\tfor _, claimStatus := range podScheduling.Status.ResourceClaims {\n734: \t\t\tif sliceContains(claimStatus.UnsuitableNodes, podScheduling.Spec.SelectedNode) {\n735: \t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"PodSchedulingContext has unsuitable selected node, schedule immediately\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"selectedNode\", podScheduling.Spec.SelectedNode, \"podResourceName\", claimStatus.Name)\n736: \t\t\t\treturn framework.Queue, nil\n737: \t\t\t}\n738: \t\t}\n739: \t}\n740: \n741: \t// Update with only the spec modified?\n742: \tif oldPodScheduling != nil &&\n743: \t\t!apiequality.Semantic.DeepEqual(&oldPodScheduling.Spec, &podScheduling.Spec) &&\n744: \t\tapiequality.Semantic.DeepEqual(&oldPodScheduling.Status, &podScheduling.Status) {\n745: \t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"PodSchedulingContext has only the scheduler spec changes, ignore the update\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod))\n746: \t\treturn framework.QueueSkip, nil\n747: \t}\n748: \n749: \t// Once we get here, all changes which are known to require special responses\n750: \t// have been checked for. Whatever the change was, we don't know exactly how\n751: \t// to handle it and thus return Queue. This will cause the\n752: \t// scheduler to treat the event as if no event hint callback had been provided.\n753: \t// Developers who want to investigate this can enable a diff at log level 6.\n754: \tif loggerV := logger.V(6); loggerV.Enabled() {\n755: \t\tloggerV.Info(\"PodSchedulingContext for pod with unknown changes, maybe schedule\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"podSchedulingDiff\", cmp.Diff(oldPodScheduling, podScheduling))\n756: \t} else {\n757: \t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"PodSchedulingContext for pod with unknown changes, maybe schedule\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod))\n758: \t}\n759: \treturn framework.Queue, nil\n760: \n761: }\n762: \n763: func podSchedulingHasClaimInfo(podScheduling *resourcev1alpha2.PodSchedulingContext, podResourceName string) bool {\n764: \tfor _, claimStatus := range podScheduling.Status.ResourceClaims {\n765: \t\tif claimStatus.Name == podResourceName {\n766: \t\t\treturn true\n767: \t\t}\n768: \t}\n769: \treturn false\n770: }\n771: \n772: func sliceContains(hay []string, needle string) bool {\n773: \tfor _, item := range hay {\n774: \t\tif item == needle {\n775: \t\t\treturn true\n776: \t\t}\n777: \t}\n778: \treturn false\n779: }\n780: \n781: // podResourceClaims returns the ResourceClaims for all pod.Spec.PodResourceClaims.\n782: func (pl *dynamicResources) podResourceClaims(pod *v1.Pod) ([]*resourcev1alpha2.ResourceClaim, error) {\n783: \tclaims := make([]*resourcev1alpha2.ResourceClaim, 0, len(pod.Spec.ResourceClaims))\n784: \tif err := pl.foreachPodResourceClaim(pod, func(_ string, claim *resourcev1alpha2.ResourceClaim) {\n785: \t\t// We store the pointer as returned by the lister. **Notably absent**: ResourceSlice\n\n## Root Cause\n\n### File 1: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n- **Function**: Global GVK constant definitions\n- **Lines**: 68-96\n- **Issue**: Missing ResourceSlice GVK constant\n- **Impact**: Cannot reference framework.ResourceSlice in event handler code\n\n### File 2: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n- **Function**: `addAllEventHandlers()`\n- **Lines**: 395-543 (switch statement)\n- **Issue**: Missing `case framework.ResourceSlice:` block\n- **Impact**: ResourceSlice changes never trigger scheduler queue re-evaluation\n\n### File 3: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n- **Function**: `EventsToRegister()`\n- **Lines**: 381-412\n- **Issue**: No event registration for ResourceSlice despite it being critical for DRA scheduling\n- **Impact**: DRA plugin doesn't listen for ResourceSlice events, so pods waiting for resources aren't re-evaluated\n\n## Why This Bug Occurs\n\n**The Race Condition:**\n\n1. **Pod created \u2192 DRA driver hasn't started yet** (common scenario):\n   - Pod enters scheduling\n   - PreFilter plugin checks for ResourceSlices but finds none\n   - Scheduler returns \"cannot allocate all claims\" error (Unschedulable status)\n   - Pod moved to unschedulable queue\n\n2. **DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlice objects**:\n   - ResourceSlice Add events fire\n   - But NO event handler is registered for ResourceSlice\n   - Event is silently dropped\n   - Scheduler queue is never notified\n   - **Pod stays in unschedulable queue forever**\n\n3. **If DRA driver starts first** (working scenario):\n   - ResourceSlices already exist when pod arrives\n   - Scheduling succeeds immediately\n   - No race condition\n\n**Why Pods Get Stuck:**\n\nThe scheduler uses an event-driven re-queuing architecture. When a pod fails scheduling:\n- The failure is recorded with which plugins rejected it\n- The pod is moved to the unschedulable queue\n- When a triggering event occurs (e.g., \"ResourceSlice added\"), ALL pods are re-queued\n- The plugin's `EventsToRegister()` declares which events should trigger re-evaluation\n\nSince ResourceSlice is not in:\n1. The GVK constants list\n2. The event handler registration switch\n3. The DynamicResources plugin's EventsToRegister list\n\nResourceSlice events never trigger pod re-evaluation. The pods remain permanently stuck in the unschedulable queue.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n**Location**: After line 96 (after ResourceClassParameters)\n\n```diff\n \tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n \tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"resource.k8s.io/ResourceSlice\"\n\n \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### Fix 2: Add ResourceSlice Event Handler Registration\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n**Location**: In `addAllEventHandlers()` function after ResourceClassParameters case (after line 483)\n\n```diff\n \tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n \t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n \t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n \t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n \t\t\t); err != nil {\n \t\t\t\treturn err\n \t\t\t}\n \t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n \t\t}\n+\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t}\n \tcase framework.StorageClass:\n```\n\n### Fix 3: Add ResourceSlice Event Registration in DRA Plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n**Location**: In `EventsToRegister()` method after ResourceClass event (after line 410)\n\n```diff\n \tevents := []framework.ClusterEventWithHint{\n \t\t// Changes for claim or class parameters creation may make pods\n \t\t// schedulable which depend on claims using those parameters.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimParametersChange},\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClassParametersChange},\n\n \t\t// Allocation is tracked in ResourceClaims, so any changes may make the pods schedulable.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaim, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimChange},\n \t\t// When a driver has provided additional information, a pod waiting for that information\n \t\t// may be schedulable.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterPodSchedulingContextChange},\n \t\t// A resource might depend on node labels for topology filtering.\n \t\t// A new or updated node may make pods schedulable.\n \t\t//\n \t\t// A note about UpdateNodeTaint event:\n \t\t// NodeAdd QueueingHint isn't ActionType: framework.Add | framework.UpdateNodeLabel | framework.UpdateNodeTaint}},\n \t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlices contain the actual available resources on nodes.\n+\t\t// New or **Notably absent**: ResourceSlice\n\n## Root Cause\n\n### File 1: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n- **Function**: Global GVK constant definitions\n- **Lines**: 68-96\n- **Issue**: Missing ResourceSlice GVK constant\n- **Impact**: Cannot reference framework.ResourceSlice in event handler code\n\n### File 2: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n- **Function**: `addAllEventHandlers()`\n- **Lines**: 395-543 (switch statement)\n- **Issue**: Missing `case framework.ResourceSlice:` block\n- **Impact**: ResourceSlice changes never trigger scheduler queue re-evaluation\n\n### File 3: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n- **Function**: `EventsToRegister()`\n- **Lines**: 381-412\n- **Issue**: No event registration for ResourceSlice despite it being critical for DRA scheduling\n- **Impact**: DRA plugin doesn't listen for ResourceSlice events, so pods waiting for resources aren't re-evaluated\n\n## Why This Bug Occurs\n\n**The Race Condition:**\n\n1. **Pod created \u2192 DRA driver hasn't started yet** (common scenario):\n   - Pod enters scheduling\n   - PreFilter plugin checks for ResourceSlices but finds none\n   - Scheduler returns \"cannot allocate all claims\" error (Unschedulable status)\n   - Pod moved to unschedulable queue\n\n2. **DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlice objects**:\n   - ResourceSlice Add events fire\n   - But NO event handler is registered for ResourceSlice\n   - Event is silently dropped\n   - Scheduler queue is never notified\n   - **Pod stays in unschedulable queue forever**\n\n3. **If DRA driver starts first** (working scenario):\n   - ResourceSlices already exist when pod arrives\n   - Scheduling succeeds immediately\n   - No race condition\n\n**Why Pods Get Stuck:**\n\nThe scheduler uses an event-driven re-queuing architecture. When a pod fails scheduling:\n- The failure is recorded with which plugins rejected it\n- The pod is moved to the unschedulable queue\n- When a triggering event occurs (e.g., \"ResourceSlice added\"), ALL pods are re-queued\n- The plugin's `EventsToRegister()` declares which events should trigger re-evaluation\n\nSince ResourceSlice is not in:\n1. The GVK constants list\n2. The event handler registration switch\n3. The DynamicResources plugin's EventsToRegister list\n\nResourceSlice events never trigger pod re-evaluation. The pods remain permanently stuck in the unschedulable queue.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n**Location**: After line 96 (after ResourceClassParameters)\n\n```diff\n \tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n \tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"resource.k8s.io/ResourceSlice\"\n\n \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### Fix 2: Add ResourceSlice Event Handler Registration\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n**Location**: In `addAllEventHandlers()` function after ResourceClassParameters case (after line 483)\n\n```diff\n \tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n \t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n \t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n \t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n \t\t\t); err != nil {\n \t\t\t\treturn err\n \t\t\t}\n \t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n \t\t}\n+\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t}\n \tcase framework.StorageClass:\n```\n\n### Fix 3: Add ResourceSlice Event Registration in DRA Plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n**Location**: In `EventsToRegister()` method after ResourceClass event (after line 410)\n\n```diff\n \tevents := []framework.ClusterEventWithHint{\n \t\t// Changes for claim or class parameters creation may make pods\n \t\t// schedulable which depend on claims using those parameters.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimParametersChange},\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClassParametersChange},\n\n \t\t// Allocation is tracked in ResourceClaims, so any changes may make the pods schedulable.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaim, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimChange},\n \t\t// When a driver has provided additional information, a pod waiting for that information\n \t\t// may be schedulable.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterPodSchedulingContextChange},\n \t\t// A resource might depend on node labels for topology filtering.\n \t\t// A new or updated node may make pods schedulable.\n \t\t//\n \t\t// A note about UpdateNodeTaint event:\n \t\t// NodeAdd QueueingHint isn't always called because of the internal feature called preCheck.\n \t\t// As a common problematic scenario,\n \t\t// when a node is added but not ready, NodeAdd event is filtered out by preCheck and doesn't arrive.\n \t\t// In such cases, this plugin may miss some events that actually make pods schedulable.\n \t\t// As a workaround, we add UpdateNodeTaint event to catch the case.\n \t\t// We can remove UpdateNodeTaint when we remove the preCheck feature.\n \t\t// See: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/110175\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.UpdateNodeLabel | framework.UpdateNodeTaint}},\n \t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlices contain the actual available resources on nodes.\n+\t\t// New or updated slices may make pods waiting for DRA resources schedulable.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n \t}\n \treturn events\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### What Happens Without The Fix\n\n1. **Pod with DRA claims created** (no ResourceSlices exist yet):\n   - Scheduler runs PreFilter plugins\n   - DynamicResources plugin checks for resources\n   - No ResourceSlices found \u2192 \"cannot allocate claims\"\n   - Pod marked Unschedulable(UnschedulableAndUnresolvable)\n   - Pod moved to unschedulable queue\n\n2. **DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlices**:\n   - API server fires ResourceSlice Add event\n   - **NO event handler registered** \u2192 event dropped silently\n   - Scheduler queue is never woken up\n   - Pods remain in unschedulable queue\n\n3. **Scheduler state**:\n   - Unschedulable queue contains pod\n   - Pod will never be retried (unless manually deleted/updated)\n   - Cluster appears deadlocked from user perspective\n\n### What Happens With The Fix\n\n1. **Pod with DRA claims created** (no ResourceSlices exist yet):\n   - Same as before: Pod marked Unschedulable and moved to queue\n   - Pod marked with `Diagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins: [DynamicResources]`\n\n2. **DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlices**:\n   - API server fires ResourceSlice Add event\n   - **Event handler registered** at line 484-492 (eventhandlers.go)\n   - Handler calls `scheduler.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, evt, nil, obj, nil)`\n   - **Dynamic resources plugin has ResourceSlice in EventsToRegister()** at line 414 (dynamicresources.go)\n   - Queue's queueing hint logic checks: pod failed due to DynamicResources plugin?\n   - If yes, ResourceSlice event is relevant \u2192 pod moved back to active queue\n   - Pod retried immediately on next scheduling cycle\n   - Scheduling succeeds (now ResourceSlices ResourceSlices already exist when pod arrives\n   - Scheduling succeeds immediately\n   - No race condition\n\n**Why Pods Get Stuck:**\n\nThe scheduler uses an event-driven re-queuing architecture. When a pod fails scheduling:\n- The failure is recorded with which plugins rejected it\n- The pod is moved to the unschedulable queue\n- When a triggering event occurs (e.g., \"ResourceSlice added\"), ALL pods are re-queued\n- The plugin's `EventsToRegister()` declares which events should trigger re-evaluation\n\nSince ResourceSlice is not in:\n1. The GVK constants list\n2. The event handler registration switch\n3. The DynamicResources plugin's EventsToRegister list\n\nResourceSlice events never trigger pod re-evaluation. The pods remain permanently stuck in the unschedulable queue.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n**Location**: After line 96 (after ResourceClassParameters)\n\n```diff\n \tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n \tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\nNote: ResourceSlice uses no group prefix (like other resource.k8s.io resources: PodSchedulingContext, ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, etc.) while storage.k8s.io resources use the \"storage.k8s.io/\" prefix.\n\n### Fix 2: Add ResourceSlice Event Handler Registration\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n**Location**: In `addAllEventHandlers()` function after ResourceClassParameters case (after line 483)\n\n```diff\n \tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n \t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n \t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n \t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n \t\t\t); err != nil {\n \t\t\t\treturn err\n \t\t\t}\n \t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n \t\t}\n+\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t}\n \tcase framework.StorageClass:\n```\n\n### Fix 3: Add ResourceSlice Event Registration in DRA Plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n**Location**: In `EventsToRegister()` method after ResourceClass event (after line 410)\n\n```diff\n \tevents := []framework.ClusterEventWithHint{\n \t\t// Changes for claim or class parameters creation may make pods\n \t\t// schedulable which depend on claims using those parameters.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimParametersChange},\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClassParametersChange},\n\n \t\t// Allocation is tracked in ResourceClaims, so any changes may make the pods schedulable.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaim, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimChange},\n \t\t// When a driver has provided additional information, a pod waiting for that information\n \t\t// may be schedulable.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterPodSchedulingContextChange},\n \t\t// A resource might depend on node labels for topology filtering.\n \t\t// A new or updated node may make pods schedulable.\n \t\t//\n \t\t// A note about UpdateNodeTaint event:\n \t\t// NodeAdd QueueingHint isn't always called because of the internal feature called preCheck.\n \t\t// As a common problematic scenario,\n \t\t// when a node is added but not ready, NodeAdd event is filtered out by preCheck and doesn't arrive.\n \t\t// In such cases, this plugin may miss some events that actually make pods schedulable.\n \t\t// As a workaround, we add UpdateNodeTaint event to catch the case.\n \t\t// We can remove UpdateNodeTaint when we remove the preCheck feature.\n \t\t// See: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/110175\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.UpdateNodeLabel | framework.UpdateNodeTaint}},\n \t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlices contain the actual available resources on nodes.\n+\t\t// New or updated slices may make pods waiting for DRA resources schedulable.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n \t}\n \treturn events\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### What Happens Without The Fix\n\n1. **Pod with DRA claims created** (no ResourceSlices exist yet):\n   - Scheduler runs PreFilter plugins\n   - DynamicResources plugin checks for resources\n   - No ResourceSlices found \u2192 \"cannot allocate claims\"\n   - Pod marked Unschedulable(UnschedulableAndUnresolvable)\n   - Pod moved to unschedulable queue\n\n2. **DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlices**:\n   - API server fires ResourceSlice Add event\n   - **NO event handler registered** \u2192 event dropped silently\n   - Scheduler queue is never woken up\n   - Pods remain in unschedulable queue\n\n3. **Scheduler state**:\n   - Unschedulable queue contains pod\n   - Pod will never be retried (unless manually deleted/updated)\n   - Cluster appears deadlocked from user perspective\n\n### What Happens With The Fix\n\n1. **Pod with DRA claims created** (no ResourceSlices exist yet):\n   - Same as before: Pod plugin?\n   - If yes, ResourceSlice event is relevant \u2192 pod moved back to active queue\n   - Pod retried immediately on next scheduling cycle\n   - Scheduling succeeds (now ResourceSlices exist)\n\n### Why All Three Changes Are Necessary\n\n- **Fix 1** (GVK constant): Allows code to reference `framework.ResourceSlice`\n- **Fix 2** (event handler): Wires ResourceSlice events into the 1. WRITE /logs/agent/solution.md
# Kubernetes Scheduler DRA ResourceSlice Event Handler Bug - Root Cause Analysis

## Files Examined

1. **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** — Entry point for pod scheduling, calls schedulingCycle() which may fail due to missing DRA resources
2. **pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go** — Event handler registration mechanism where ResourceSlice handler is missing
3. **pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go** — GVK constants definition where ResourceSlice GVK is missing
4. **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go** — DRA plugin that registers events but excludes ResourceSlice

## Dependency Chain

1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go::ScheduleOne()` at line 66
   - Pod enters scheduling cycle
   - May fail with "cannot allocate all claims" error
   - Pod marked Unschedulable but never re-queued

2. **Error handling path**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go::schedulingCycle()` at line 139
   - Calls `SchedulePod()` at line 149
   - If pod fails to schedule (err != nil at line 150), checks for PostFilter plugins
   - Returns status with Unschedulable, but pod is only re-queued if events trigger queue movement

3. **Queue re-evaluation trigger**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go::addAllEventHandlers()` at line 287
   - Registers event handlers for various resource types
   - Switch statement at lines 395-543 handles specific GVK cases
   - **Bug triggered by**: Missing `case framework.ResourceSlice:` block in the switch

4. **Plugin level event registration**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go::EventsToRegister()` at line 381
   - Registers events for ResourceClaim, PodSchedulingContext, ResourceClass, etc.
   - **MISSING**: No event registration for ResourceSlice

5. **Missing GVK constant**: `pkg/schedule
... (truncated)
2. EDIT /logs/agent/solution.md
Before
### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant

**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`
**Location**: After line 96 (after ResourceClassParameters)

```diff
 	ResourceClaim           GVK = "ResourceClaim"
 	ResourceClass           GVK = "ResourceClass"
 	ResourceClaimParameters GVK = "ResourceClaimParameters"
 	ResourceClassParameters GVK = "ResourceClassParameters"
+	ResourceSlice           GVK = "resource.k8s.io/ResourceSlice"

 	// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.
```
After
### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant

**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`
**Location**: After line 96 (after ResourceClassParameters)

```diff
 	ResourceClaim           GVK = "ResourceClaim"
 	ResourceClass           GVK = "ResourceClass"
 	ResourceClaimParameters GVK = "ResourceClaimParameters"
 	ResourceClassParameters GVK = "ResourceClassParameters"
+	ResourceSlice           GVK = "ResourceSlice"

 	// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.
```

Note: ResourceSlice uses no group prefix (like other resource.k8s.io resources: PodSchedulingContext, ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, etc.) while storage.k8s.io resources use the "storage.k8s.io/" prefix.
3. EDIT /logs/agent/solution.md
Before
### What Happens With The Fix

1. **Pod with DRA claims created** (no ResourceSlices exist yet):
   - Same as before: Pod marked Unschedulable and moved to queue
   - Pod marked with `Diagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins: [DynamicResources]`

2. **DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlices**:
   - API server fires ResourceSlice Add event
   - **Event handler registered** at line 484-492 (eventhandlers.go)
   - Handler calls `scheduler.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, evt, nil, obj, nil)`
   - **Dynamic resources plugin has ResourceSlice in EventsToRegister()** at line 414 (dynamicresources.go)
   - Queue's queueing hint logic checks: pod failed due to DynamicResources plugin?
   - If yes, ResourceSlice event is relevant → pod moved back to active queue
   - Pod retried immediately on next scheduling cycle
   - Scheduling succeeds (now ResourceSlices exist)

### Why All Three Changes Are Necessary

- **Fix 1** (GVK constant): Allows code to reference `framework.ResourceSlice`
- **Fix 2** (event handler): Wires ResourceSlice events into the scheduler queue
- **Fix 3** (plugin registration): Tells the framework that DynamicResources plugin cares about ResourceSlice events, so queueing hints work correctly

Without all three, the fix is incomplete:
- Without Fix 1 & 2: Code doesn't compile/event handler never registers
- Without Fix 3: Events registered but not linked to the plugin that actually needs them
After
### What Happens With The Fix

1. **Pod with DRA claims created** (no ResourceSlices exist yet):
   - Same as before: Pod marked Unschedulable and moved to queue
   - Pod marked with `Diagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins: [DynamicResources]`

2. **DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlices**:
   - API server fires ResourceSlice Add event
   - **Event handler registered** at lines 484-492 (eventhandlers.go after Fix 2)
   - Handler calls `scheduler.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, evt, nil, obj, nil)`
   - **Dynamic resources plugin has ResourceSlice in EventsToRegister()** at line 414 (dynamicresources.go after Fix 3)
   - Queue's queueing hint logic checks: pod failed due to DynamicResources plugin?
   - If yes, ResourceSlice event is relevant → pod moved back to active queue
   - Pod retried immediately on next scheduling cycle
   - Scheduling succeeds (now ResourceSlices exist)

### Why All Three Changes Are Necessary

- **Fix 1** (GVK constant): Allows code to reference `framework.ResourceSlice`
- **Fix 2** (event handler): Wires ResourceSlice events into the scheduler queue's re-evaluation mechanism
- **Fix 3** (plugin registration): Tells the framework that DynamicResources plugin cares about ResourceSlice events, so queueing hints work correctly

Without all three, the fix is incomplete:
- Without Fix 1 & 2: Code doesn't compile/event handler never registers
- Without Fix 3: Events registered but not linked to the plugin that actually needs them, so queueing optimization fails

## Summary

The bug is a **missing event handler integration** for ResourceSlice objects in the Kubernetes scheduler's Dynamic Resource Allocation system. When a pod fails scheduling due to missing DRA resources, it gets stuck in the unschedulable queue because ResourceSli
... (truncated)
